<div id="review_10400741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10400741" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/575513-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1193250934p2/575513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10400741?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/575513-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10400741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5946616658969776798">I went through different emotions while reading this book. The first time I picked it up I read a few pages and decided I wasn't in the mood to read it. This last time I picked it up I actually thought it was a different book, but read it anyway. <br/><br/>It's interesting the way Alexie writes, combining vulgarity with such a poetic voice. The first story made me want to put the book down again, but my brother convinced me to trudge on. The second story had a bit of what I assumed my brother loved about </span>
  <span id="freeText5946616658969776798" style="display:none">I went through different emotions while reading this book. The first time I picked it up I read a few pages and decided I wasn't in the mood to read it. This last time I picked it up I actually thought it was a different book, but read it anyway. <br /><br />It's interesting the way Alexie writes, combining vulgarity with such a poetic voice. The first story made me want to put the book down again, but my brother convinced me to trudge on. The second story had a bit of what I assumed my brother loved about the book, that poetic voice that made the ugliness beautiful.<br /><br />I liked the way this collection of short stories revolved around the same characters. Some stories were written in first person, others in third. I found a few of the stories to be tiresome and a few others very enjoyable. Mostly it made me feel a little sad and wonder if all Indians really are alcoholics. My brother promised a happy ending, but I din't find it to be happy exactly. It was more a kind of contendedness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5946616658969776798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383144705" />
    <a title="Mississippi Library Commission" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6193041-mississippi-library-commission"><img alt="Mississippi Library Commission" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461076535p2/6193041.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6193041-mississippi-library-commission?shelf=diversity">diversity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6193041-mississippi-library-commission?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6193041-mississippi-library-commission?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6193041-mississippi-library-commission?shelf=staff-reads">staff-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6193041-mississippi-library-commission?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1383144705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12272027444600577094">Sherman Alexie, we want you to write more books. Want? <b>Need</b>. The stories in this book deftly bring to light America's marginalized native people. We see their love, their humor, and their pain, and it's simply beautiful. A re-read of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693208.The_Absolutely_True_Diary_of_a_Part_Time_Indian' title='The Absolutely True Diary of a Part-Time Indian by Sherman Alexie' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Absolutely True Diary of a Part-Time Indian</a> is definitely in order, but TLRATFIH is one to savor and return to again as well.</span>
  <span id="freeText12272027444600577094" style="display:none">Sherman Alexie, we want you to write more books. Want? <b>Need</b>. The stories in this book deftly bring to light America's marginalized native people. We see their love, their humor, and their pain, and it's simply beautiful. A re-read of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/693208.The_Absolutely_True_Diary_of_a_Part_Time_Indian" title="The Absolutely True Diary of a Part-Time Indian by Sherman Alexie" rel="nofollow noopener">The Absolutely True Diary of a Part-Time Indian</a> is definitely in order, but TLRATFIH is one to savor and return to again as well.</span>

<div id="review_2440340134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2440340134" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1668393-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269496818p2/1668393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2440340134?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/1668393-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2440340134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1539576533239664126">Absolutely magic. A slow-starter and I might give it 4 1/2 stars if I had the option, but really all the stories felt so damn true and lived-in; the beauty of it snuck up on me. It's crazy that stories like these still aren't really part of the general American consciousness. But I'm not really surprised. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZxExy6TjLtJNklzwN7AEe0w8ZyluvyfQ2lUt1MuLMHkEiG0twURgPOTium7X3EyckhjZn+aWo3YUFaNhzQS1hA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

His days and nights blending together in an alcoholic haze, he meets a deranged white man, picks up women and gets punched in the nose. Meanwhile, he is haunted by a past that includes the death of an older brother and an injury to his knee that multiple operations have not remedied. \n\nOut of these unpromising circumstances, Welch finds the beginnings of a kind of personal salvation. Some of the &quot;original bitches&quot; (OBs) revisit their earlier essays to reflect on their previous selves. All reveal how their lives have changed in the intervening years—whether they stayed coupled, left marriages, or had affairs; developed cancer or other physical challenges; coped with partners who strayed, died, or remained faithful; became full-time wage earners or homemakers; opened up their marriages; remained childless or became parents; or experienced other meaningful life transitions.\n\nAs a &quot;new wave&quot; of feminists begins to take center stage, this powerful, timely collection sheds a much-needed light on both past and present, offering understanding, <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14638331947625482589">Sherman J. Alexie, Jr., was born in October 1966. A Spokane/Coeur d'Alene Indian, he grew up on the Spokane Indian Reservation in Wellpinit, WA, about 50 miles northwest of Spokane, WA. Alexie has published 18 books to date. <br/>Alexie is an award-winning and prolific author and occasional comedian. Much of his writing draws on his experiences as a modern Native American. Sherman's best known works in</span>
  <span id="freeText14638331947625482589" style="display:none">Sherman J. Alexie, Jr., was born in October 1966. A Spokane/Coeur d'Alene Indian, he grew up on the Spokane Indian Reservation in Wellpinit, WA, about 50 miles northwest of Spokane, WA. Alexie has published 18 books to date. <br />Alexie is an award-winning and prolific author and occasional comedian. Much of his writing draws on his experiences as a modern Native American. Sherman's best known works include The Lone Ranger and Tonto Fistfight in Heaven, Smoke Signals, and The Absolutely True Diary of a Part-Time Indian. He lives in Seattle, Washington.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14638331947625482589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
